That retroactively explains rounds 15–20: the 'narrow vertical band of stripes in the middle of the screen' those photos captured was LVGL's centre-aligned UI widgets sitting on top of the same full-panel diagonal stripe pattern, hidden everywhere else because LVGL's black screen background also rendered as one of the 'dark' colours in the stripe cycle, blending into the panel's miscoloured 'background' state. Geometry was never broken; the panel was accepting data for the whole screen all along. The diagonal-stripes-plus-invert-on-white fingerprint is a textbook pixel-format mismatch: the panel is latching 18 bits per pixel (its ST7701S-datasheet reset default for the RGB interface, 0x3A = 0x66 / RGB666) while we drive 16 data lines. Every row picks up data at a slightly different sub-pixel phase because 16 bits / 18 bits = 0.89 pixels per PCLK from the panel's point of view; the fractional offset accumulates across each line and further accumulates from one line to the next, producing the diagonal rather than vertical stripe direction. When every DB pin is driven HIGH at once (WHITE), the 'extra' two bits the PCB leaves floating or tied to a fixed level for 16-line boards suddenly shift the panel's internal interpretation, and what was 'bright stripe on dark background' becomes 'dark stripe on bright background' — the inversion the user photographed. Fix: re-add {0x3A, {0x55}, 1, 0} into kInitCmds[] between the Command2 exit (0xFF with params {0x77,0x01,0x00,0x00,0x00}) and the SLPOUT / DISPON pair. 0x55 on 0x3A programs RGB interface to 16-bit 5-6-5: DB[15..11]=R[4..0], DB[10..5]=G[5..0], DB[4..0]=B[4..0] — which matches initRgbPanel()'s data_gpio_nums[] layout byte-for-byte. Round 19 removed COLMOD on the rationale that espressif's own esp_lcd_st7701 BSP omits it (verified true). But espressif's reference board straps IM[3:0] differently from Waveshare's ESP32-S3-Touch-LCD-2.1 — their panel power-ons into 16-bit mode already; ours power-ons into the datasheet default 0x66 (18-bit). Rounds 17 and 18 also sent 0x3A, but with wrong values or wrong GIP context: round 17 shipped 0x66 (made the 18-bit mismatch explicit instead of fixing it), round 18 shipped 0x55 (right value) but all six BK1 GIP blocks 0xE0..0xED in that table were wrong, so the gate drivers misbehaved and hid the COLMOD fix behind a separate failure. Round 19 threw out both the bad GIP values AND the 0x55 COLMOD. Round 22 combines round 19's verbatim-espressif GIP with round 18's 0x55 COLMOD — the combination we have never actually shipped. Single-line change in src/display/st7701_panel.cpp: new 0x3A entry inserted right before SLPOUT. A long-form comment block above the entry records the round-22 narrative so the next time someone cross-references espressif's BSP and decides COLMOD is redundant, they'll see why it matters for this specific Waveshare panel module. Nothing else changes — round 21's colour-bar diagnostic stays in src/Ui.cpp so we can immediately see whether round 22 produced the expected 'full-screen solid red, then solid green, then solid blue, then solid white' sequence. If that's what the next photos show: COLMOD was it, round 23 removes the colour-bar diagnostic and verifies LVGL renders the Overview page cleanly. If the diagonal stripes survive 0x55: the next suspect is the ESP-IDF 4.4.7 RGB peripheral's interaction with the ST7701's clock/sample-edge conventions — round 23 would try pclk_active_neg back to 1 (we flipped it 1->0 in round 16 but only ever tested via LVGL, where the centred-content masking hid the diagonal pattern), and failing that, step data_width from 16 down to 8 to see whether the peripheral is mis-routing the high byte. Historical context preserved from round 21: insert a boot-time colour-bar diagnostic to disambiguate three distinct hypotheses for the round-17..20 persistent stripe pattern. Round 20 shipped an RGB-bus-timing overhaul (PCLK 14→10 MHz, hsync pulse 8→10, hsync back porch 10→20, hsync front porch 50→20, vsync pulse 2→10, vsync back porch 18→10, vsync front porch 8→10) and the photo came back visually identical to rounds 18/19 — uniform dark blue/purple field with a column of bright blue/cyan vertical stripes compressed into the middle ~1/3 of the round panel. That's now three radically different init sequences (rounds 13–16 stitched, round 17/18 + COLMOD, round 19+ verbatim espressif port) and two very different RGB timing configurations (rounds 14–19 FatihErtugral-style, round 20 Espressif-typical) all producing the SAME visual symptom. The invariance across such wide software changes is the key data point: whatever is wrong is downstream of both the init protocol and the RGB timing — either in geometry (the panel is only receiving data for a subset of its horizontal pixels) or in bit-lane mapping (black rendering as blue and white rendering as cyan/blue due to miswired RGB data pins). A re-read of src/Ui.cpp on the way to round 21 surfaced a plausible third explanation: every widget on the Overview page (the default page that loads at boot) aligns to LV_ALIGN_TOP_MID / LV_ALIGN_CENTER / LV_ALIGN_BOTTOM_MID — the 280x280 wind compass at TOP_MID, the 48pt SOG label at BOTTOM_MID -80, the AWS value at CENTER, the HDG/COG line at BOTTOM_MID -15. All visible LVGL-drawn pixels sit in a narrow vertical column in the middle of the 480-wide screen. If the RGB bit lanes are miswired such that black (0x0000) happens to render as a dark blue/purple and white (0xFFFF) happens to render as bright cyan/blue, the photos from rounds 15–20 are exactly what you'd see: dark-blue field everywhere LVGL drew the screen background, bright-blue stripes everywhere LVGL drew the '--' placeholder text, perfectly centred. That's now plausible enough to be worth testing directly. Round 21 inserts a solid-colour test sequence into src/Ui.cpp::ui::begin() immediately after the successful g_panel.begin() call and BEFORE lv_init(), so it runs against a clean RGB bus with no LVGL involvement. The sequence is g_panel.fillColor(0xF800) → delay(2000) → 0x07E0 → 0x001F → 0xFFFF → 0x0000, giving 2 s of RED, GREEN, BLUE, WHITE then 1 s of BLACK before LVGL takes over. Each fillColor writes a full PSRAM row of the raw uint16_t then repeats it PANEL_HEIGHT times via esp_lcd_panel_draw_bitmap, bypassing LVGL entirely. The photo from each phase maps cleanly onto a failure mode: (a) if each phase fills the ENTIRE round panel with the named solid colour → RGB bus and panel geometry are both healthy, the 'middle stripe band' we've been photographing was just LVGL's centred UI, and round 22 focuses purely on colour mapping (which colour comes out as what); (b) if each phase shows only a narrow middle band of the named colour with the rest in power-on state → geometry is actually broken, the panel is accepting data for only a subset of horizontal pixels per line, and round 22 attacks horizontal addressing (partial-display mode bit in 0xC0 byte 2 SCN, interface-mode mismatch between panel strapping and our 16-line drive, or an IDF-level hactive calculation error); (c) if the colour filled does NOT match what appears on screen (RED fill shows BLUE etc.) → RGB data pins are cross-wired, and the specific 'fill colour → visible colour' table from the photos tells us exactly which five-entry R/G/B sub-block in data_gpio_nums[] to shuffle. This is a one-reboot-cycle, no-scope-needed diagnostic that uniquely identifies which of those three distinct hypotheses we're in, and determines round 22's direction. Only change in this round: ~30 lines inserted into src/Ui.cpp between ST7701.begin() and lv_init(). No src/display/ changes, no platformio.ini changes, no init-table or timing changes — round 20's Espressif-typical timings and round-19's verbatim-espressif init are both preserved. Historical context preserved from round 20: pivot from init-sequence edits to RGB-bus timing. Round 19 shipped a verbatim port of espressif's ST7701 init sequence and the display output did not change from round 18 — same uniform-blue background, same column of green+blue stripes compressed into the middle ~1/3 of the screen. The fact that a completely different init sequence produced an identical visual symptom is diagnostic: the problem is not in what commands we send to the panel, it is in HOW we drive the 16 RGB data lines and their sync/porch signals afterward. Round 20 retunes the RGB peripheral in two parts. (a) PCLK drops from 14 MHz to 10 MHz in display_pins.h::RGB_PCLK_HZ. Rounds 14–19 used 14 MHz because that's what FatihErtugral's working config for the sibling Waveshare 2.8" ST7701 board ships; but on our 2.1" 480×480 panel 14 MHz is apparently outrunning the source-driver sampling window given our generous front porch. 10 MHz is well inside the ST7701S-datasheet-guaranteed band (~3 MHz to ~20 MHz) and biases for 'works' over 'max refresh'. We can step back up to 12–14 MHz once the image is coherent. (b) Porches move from FatihErtugral's values to Espressif's Waveshare-BSP typical values. Specifically: hsync_pulse_width 8→10, hsync_back_porch 10→20, hsync_front_porch 50→20, vsync_pulse_width 2→10, vsync_back_porch 18→10, vsync_front_porch 8→10 in st7701_panel.cpp::initRgbPanel(). The single largest delta is hsync_front_porch dropping from 50 to 20 — 50 was ~5x the value Espressif uses for comparable 480×480 ST7701 BSPs and is the strongest suspect for why the panel's HSYNC resync arrives too late per line, with pixels at the end of one line bleeding into the start of the next. The new porch+PCLK combo gives total 530×510 clocks per frame @ 10 MHz = 37 Hz refresh (down from 50 Hz); flickery on a bench but harmless for bring-up. Init sequence is untouched from round 19 (verbatim espressif port). Pin order, backlight, and TCA9554 reset sequence all unchanged. If round 20 visibly changes the stripe pattern — width, shape, or position — timing was involved and round 21 can fine-tune from there. If round 20 shows no change at all (same as rounds 18/19), timing is not the issue and the suspect shifts to pin order or LV_COLOR_16_SWAP polarity; round 21 would then reverse data_gpio_nums to test whether the ESP-IDF 4.4.7 RGB peripheral puts bit 0 on the last array slot rather than the first. Historical context preserved from round 19: that round replaced our round-13 init table (stitched from Nicolai-Electronics + generic ST7701S datasheet) with a verbatim port of espressif/esp-iot-solution/esp_lcd_st7701_rgb.c::vendor_specific_init_default[]. Key fixes in that port were (1) BK3 entry via 0xFF {...,0x13} instead of a stray MIPI NORON, (2) entire 0xE0..0xED GIP block replaced with espressif's known-good values, (3) dropped the 0x3A COLMOD addition from rounds 17/18. None of those changes moved the visual symptom, which is what triggered the round-20 pivot. Round 18's photo showed a uniform blue background with a vertical column of green+blue stripes spanning the middle ~1/3 of the screen — a textbook gate-in-panel (GIP) timing mismatch where most columns of the panel's source drivers never get the right gate pulse and stay in their power-on blue state, while a narrow band actually scans the data we send. Rounds 13–18 used an init table stitched together from Nicolai-Electronics/esp32-component-st7701 + the generic ST7701S datasheet sequence; cross-checking that table against espressif's known-good sequence (pulled from the current master of esp-iot-solution's esp_lcd_st7701 driver) surfaced three systemic problems beyond individual byte differences: (1) Our init opened with '0xFF {0x77,0x01,0x00,0x00,0x00}' then sent '0x13' as a standalone command. We intended 0x13 as a Command2 BK3 selector but the wire bits were the MIPI standard NORON (Normal Display On). Espressif opens with '0xFF {0x77,0x01,0x00,0x00,0x13}' — BK3 entered via the 0xFF parameter — then sends '0xEF {0x08}' in BK3. Our 0xEF landed in normal mode where the command has no effect. (2) The entire 0xE0..0xED GIP block differed. GIP values are what tell the gate drivers when to pulse each row; wrong values → rows that never activate → the mid-band stripe. Espressif's values are the known-good ones for the 480x480 Waveshare ST7701 family. Our 0xB0/0xB1 (BK0 positive/negative gamma) and the BK1 power-rail constants (0xB0 VOP 0x5D→0x8D, 0xB1 VCOM 0x2D→0x48, 0xB2 0x07→0x89, 0xB5 0x08→0x49, 0xB8 0x20→0x32) were also wrong, and an 0xEF 6-byte source-timing fine-trim block in BK1 was missing entirely. (3) Rounds 17 and 18 added a 0x3A COLMOD command (0x66 then 0x55) on the theory that pixel-format was wrong; espressif OMITS 0x3A entirely because the panel's power-on default pixel format is correct for its hardware strapping (IM[3:0] pins on the panel module select 16-bit RGB interface mode). Explicitly setting a non-default COLMOD silently misaligns bits on the RGB bus, which is consistent with the stripe pattern persisting across both 0x66 and 0x55 attempts. Round 19 drops the 0x3A addition. Also removed: the stray '{0x13, {}, 0, 0}' NORON send, the '0xB9 {0x10}' line that isn't in the reference. Also in st7701_panel.cpp: kCmdNoron constant deleted (no longer used), kCmdDispon post-delay changed from 50 ms to 0 ms per espressif. Only the init table changed this round — RGB timings, pin order, backlight, and TCA9554 reset sequence all stay exactly as round 18. If round 19 still stripes, the suspect shifts from 'software init' to 'RGB bus / timing' and round 20 should pivot to: (a) reversing data_gpio_nums pin order (some ESP-IDF 4.4.x builds put bit 0 on the LAST data_gpio_nums slot, not the first), (b) widening hsync_back_porch from 10 to 20 and reducing hsync_front_porch from 50 to 20 to match Espressif's typical 480x480 ST7701 timings, (c) dropping PCLK from 14 MHz to 10 MHz to rule out bus-bandwidth issues. Round 17 added the COLMOD command for the first time (rounds 13–16 had omitted it) and the stripe pattern's dominant colour shifted from 'mostly blue' in round 16 to 'more green and blue' in round 17 — evidence the panel IS responding to COLMOD, but 0x66 was the wrong value for our wiring. 0x66 is what espressif/esp-iot-solution's ST7701 driver uses, but espressif's reference board wires 18 data lines; Waveshare's ESP32-S3-Touch-LCD-2.1 only has 16 (B0..B4, G0..G5, R0..R4). When COLMOD=0x66 the ST7701 expects DB[17..12]=R, DB[11..6]=G, DB[5..0]=B; driving only DB[15..0] means the bit positions shift — our pixel's R MSB (bit 15) lands in the panel's R3 slot, R LSB (bit 11) lands in G5, G MSB (bit 10) lands in G4, etc. That cross-channel bit-shift is exactly the pattern that produces repeating-but-mis-coloured vertical stripes instead of coherent pixels. COLMOD=0x55 sets both the RGB (DPI) and MCU (DBI) interfaces to 16-bit 5-6-5 mode, which matches our 16 data lines exactly: DB[15..11]=R[4..0], DB[10..5]=G[5..0], DB[4..0]=B[4..0] — the natural RGB565 layout the ESP32 RGB peripheral puts on the wire with LV_COLOR_DEPTH=16 and LV_COLOR_16_SWAP=1. The ST7701S datasheet section 10.2.19 lists 0x55 as valid; LovyanGFX's config for Waveshare 16-line ST7701 boards uses it too. Single-byte change: in src/display/st7701_panel.cpp::kInitCmds[], {0x3A, {0x66}, 1, 0} becomes {0x3A, {0x55}, 1, 0}. The long-form comment above the entry now explains the 18bpp-vs-16bpp mismatch in full so the next developer doesn't flip it back to 0x66 chasing the espressif reference. Round 17 context preserved: that round also corrected 0xC0 display-line setting from 0x63 (800 lines) to 0x3B (480 lines) using the (NL+1)*8 formula — that fix stays in place since the 800-line mis-programming was independently wrong. - **2026-04-24** — Display bring-up round 22: re-add the 0x3A COLMOD command with value 0x55 (16-bit RGB565 on the RGB interface). Round 21's colour-bar diagnostic produced the cleanest signal we've had since round 13. With the full-screen RED/GREEN/BLUE/WHITE/BLACK fill bypassing LVGL entirely, the photo showed DIAGONAL stripes running across the WHOLE 480x480 round panel on every solid-colour phase, with the stripe pattern INVERTING when the WHITE phase (0xFFFF — every DB pin HIGH) ran. That retroactively explains rounds 15–20: the 'narrow vertical band of stripes in the middle of the screen' those photos captured was LVGL's centre-aligned UI widgets sitting on top of the same full-panel diagonal stripe pattern, hidden everywhere else because LVGL's black screen background also rendered as one of the 'dark' colours in the stripe cycle, blending into the panel's miscoloured 'background' state. Geometry was never broken; the panel was accepting data for the whole screen all along. The diagonal-stripes-plus-invert-on-white fingerprint is a textbook pixel-format mismatch: the panel is latching 18 bits per pixel (its ST7701S-datasheet reset default for the RGB interface, 0x3A = 0x66 / RGB666) while we drive 16 data lines. Every row picks up data at a slightly different sub-pixel phase because 16 bits / 18 bits = 0.89 pixels per PCLK from the panel's point of view; the fractional offset accumulates across each line and further accumulates from one line to the next, producing the diagonal rather than vertical stripe direction. When every DB pin is driven HIGH at once (WHITE), the 'extra' two bits the PCB leaves floating or tied to a fixed level for 16-line boards suddenly shift the panel's internal interpretation, and what was 'bright stripe on dark background' becomes 'dark stripe on bright background' — the inversion the user photographed. Fix: re-add {0x3A, {0x55}, 1, 0} into kInitCmds[] between the Command2 exit (0xFF with params {0x77,0x01,0x00,0x00,0x00}) and the SLPOUT / DISPON pair. 0x55 on 0x3A programs RGB interface to 16-bit 5-6-5: DB[15..11]=R[4..0], DB[10..5]=G[5..0], DB[4..0]=B[4..0] — which matches initRgbPanel()'s data_gpio_nums[] layout byte-for-byte. Round 19 removed COLMOD on the rationale that espressif's own esp_lcd_st7701 BSP omits it (verified true). But espressif's reference board straps IM[3:0] differently from Waveshare's ESP32-S3-Touch-LCD-2.1 — their panel power-ons into 16-bit mode already; ours power-ons into the datasheet default 0x66 (18-bit). Rounds 17 and 18 also sent 0x3A, but with wrong values or wrong GIP context: round 17 shipped 0x66 (made the 18-bit mismatch explicit instead of fixing it), round 18 shipped 0x55 (right value) but all six BK1 GIP blocks 0xE0..0xED in that table were wrong, so the gate drivers misbehaved and hid the COLMOD fix behind a separate failure. Round 19 threw out both the bad GIP values AND the 0x55 COLMOD. Round 22 combines round 19's verbatim-espressif GIP with round 18's 0x55 COLMOD — the combination we have never actually shipped. Single-line change in src/display/st7701_panel.cpp: new 0x3A entry inserted right before SLPOUT. A long-form comment block above the entry records the round-22 narrative so the next time someone cross-references espressif's BSP and decides COLMOD is redundant, they'll see why it matters for this specific Waveshare panel module. Nothing else changes — round 21's colour-bar diagnostic stays in src/Ui.cpp so we can immediately see whether round 22 produced the expected 'full-screen solid red, then solid green, then solid blue, then solid white' sequence. If that's what the next photos show: COLMOD was it, round 23 removes the colour-bar diagnostic and verifies LVGL renders the Overview page cleanly. If the diagonal stripes survive 0x55: the next suspect is the ESP-IDF 4.4.7 RGB peripheral's interaction with the ST7701's clock/sample-edge conventions — round 23 would try pclk_active_neg back to 1 (we flipped it 1->0 in round 16 but only ever tested via LVGL, where the centred-content masking hid the diagonal pattern), and failing that, step data_width from 16 down to 8 to see whether the peripheral is mis-routing the high byte. Historical context preserved from round 21: insert a boot-time colour-bar diagnostic to disambiguate three distinct hypotheses for the round-17..20 persistent stripe pattern. Round 20 shipped an RGB-bus-timing overhaul (PCLK 14→10 MHz, hsync pulse 8→10, hsync back porch 10→20, hsync front porch 50→20, vsync pulse 2→10, vsync back porch 18→10, vsync front porch 8→10) and the photo came back visually identical to rounds 18/19 — uniform dark blue/purple field with a column of bright blue/cyan vertical stripes compressed into the middle ~1/3 of the round panel. That's now three radically different init sequences (rounds 13–16 stitched, round 17/18 + COLMOD, round 19+ verbatim espressif port) and two very different RGB timing configurations (rounds 14–19 FatihErtugral-style, round 20 Espressif-typical) all producing the SAME visual symptom. The invariance across such wide software changes is the key data point: whatever is wrong is downstream of both the init protocol and the RGB timing — either in geometry (the panel is only receiving data for a subset of its horizontal pixels) or in bit-lane mapping (black rendering as blue and white rendering as cyan/blue due to miswired RGB data pins). A re-read of src/Ui.cpp on the way to round 21 surfaced a plausible third explanation: every widget on the Overview page (the default page that loads at boot) aligns to LV_ALIGN_TOP_MID / LV_ALIGN_CENTER / LV_ALIGN_BOTTOM_MID — the 280x280 wind compass at TOP_MID, the 48pt SOG label at BOTTOM_MID -80, the AWS value at CENTER, the HDG/COG line at BOTTOM_MID -15. All visible LVGL-drawn pixels sit in a narrow vertical column in the middle of the 480-wide screen. If the RGB bit lanes are miswired such that black (0x0000) happens to render as a dark blue/purple and white (0xFFFF) happens to render as bright cyan/blue, the photos from rounds 15–20 are exactly what you'd see: dark-blue field everywhere LVGL drew the screen background, bright-blue stripes everywhere LVGL drew the '--' placeholder text, perfectly centred. That's now plausible enough to be worth testing directly. Round 21 inserts a solid-colour test sequence into src/Ui.cpp::ui::begin() immediately after the successful g_panel.begin() call and BEFORE lv_init(), so it runs against a clean RGB bus with no LVGL involvement. The sequence is g_panel.fillColor(0xF800) → delay(2000) → 0x07E0 → 0x001F → 0xFFFF → 0x0000, giving 2 s of RED, GREEN, BLUE, WHITE then 1 s of BLACK before LVGL takes over. Each fillColor writes a full PSRAM row of the raw uint16_t then repeats it PANEL_HEIGHT times via esp_lcd_panel_draw_bitmap, bypassing LVGL entirely. The photo from each phase maps cleanly onto a failure mode: (a) if each phase fills the ENTIRE round panel with the named solid colour → RGB bus and panel geometry are both healthy, the 'middle stripe band' we've been photographing was just LVGL's centred UI, and round 22 focuses purely on colour mapping (which colour comes out as what); (b) if each phase shows only a narrow middle band of the named colour with the rest in power-on state → geometry is actually broken, the panel is accepting data for only a subset of horizontal pixels per line, and round 22 attacks horizontal addressing (partial-display mode bit in 0xC0 byte 2 SCN, interface-mode mismatch between panel strapping and our 16-line drive, or an IDF-level hactive calculation error); (c) if the colour filled does NOT match what appears on screen (RED fill shows BLUE etc.) → RGB data pins are cross-wired, and the specific 'fill colour → visible colour' table from the photos tells us exactly which five-entry R/G/B sub-block in data_gpio_nums[] to shuffle. This is a one-reboot-cycle, no-scope-needed diagnostic that uniquely identifies which of those three distinct hypotheses we're in, and determines round 22's direction. Only change in this round: ~30 lines inserted into src/Ui.cpp between ST7701.begin() and lv_init(). No src/display/ changes, no platformio.ini changes, no init-table or timing changes — round 20's Espressif-typical timings and round-19's verbatim-espressif init are both preserved. Historical context preserved from round 20: pivot from init-sequence edits to RGB-bus timing. Round 19 shipped a verbatim port of espressif's ST7701 init sequence and the display output did not change from round 18 — same uniform-blue background, same column of green+blue stripes compressed into the middle ~1/3 of the screen. The fact that a completely different init sequence produced an identical visual symptom is diagnostic: the problem is not in what commands we send to the panel, it is in HOW we drive the 16 RGB data lines and their sync/porch signals afterward. Round 20 retunes the RGB peripheral in two parts. (a) PCLK drops from 14 MHz to 10 MHz in display_pins.h::RGB_PCLK_HZ. Rounds 14–19 used 14 MHz because that's what FatihErtugral's working config for the sibling Waveshare 2.8" ST7701 board ships; but on our 2.1" 480×480 panel 14 MHz is apparently outrunning the source-driver sampling window given our generous front porch. 10 MHz is well inside the ST7701S-datasheet-guaranteed band (~3 MHz to ~20 MHz) and biases for 'works' over 'max refresh'. We can step back up to 12–14 MHz once the image is coherent. (b) Porches move from FatihErtugral's values to Espressif's Waveshare-BSP typical values. Specifically: hsync_pulse_width 8→10, hsync_back_porch 10→20, hsync_front_porch 50→20, vsync_pulse_width 2→10, vsync_back_porch 18→10, vsync_front_porch 8→10 in st7701_panel.cpp::initRgbPanel(). The single largest delta is hsync_front_porch dropping from 50 to 20 — 50 was ~5x the value Espressif uses for comparable 480×480 ST7701 BSPs and is the strongest suspect for why the panel's HSYNC resync arrives too late per line, with pixels at the end of one line bleeding into the start of the next. The new porch+PCLK combo gives total 530×510 clocks per frame @ 10 MHz = 37 Hz refresh (down from 50 Hz); flickery on a bench but harmless for bring-up. Init sequence is untouched from round 19 (verbatim espressif port). Pin order, backlight, and TCA9554 reset sequence all unchanged. If round 20 visibly changes the stripe pattern — width, shape, or position — timing was involved and round 21 can fine-tune from there. If round 20 shows no change at all (same as rounds 18/19), timing is not the issue and the suspect shifts to pin order or LV_COLOR_16_SWAP polarity; round 21 would then reverse data_gpio_nums to test whether the ESP-IDF 4.4.7 RGB peripheral puts bit 0 on the last array slot rather than the first. Historical context preserved from round 19: that round replaced our round-13 init table (stitched from Nicolai-Electronics + generic ST7701S datasheet) with a verbatim port of espressif/esp-iot-solution/esp_lcd_st7701_rgb.c::vendor_specific_init_default[]. Key fixes in that port were (1) BK3 entry via 0xFF {...,0x13} instead of a stray MIPI NORON, (2) entire 0xE0..0xED GIP block replaced with espressif's known-good values, (3) dropped the 0x3A COLMOD addition from rounds 17/18. None of those changes moved the visual symptom, which is what triggered the round-20 pivot. Round 18's photo showed a uniform blue background with a vertical column of green+blue stripes spanning the middle ~1/3 of the screen — a textbook gate-in-panel (GIP) timing mismatch where most columns of the panel's source drivers never get the right gate pulse and stay in their power-on blue state, while a narrow band actually scans the data we send. Rounds 13–18 used an init table stitched together from Nicolai-Electronics/esp32-component-st7701 + the generic ST7701S datasheet sequence; cross-checking that table against espressif's known-good sequence (pulled from the current master of esp-iot-solution's esp_lcd_st7701 driver) surfaced three systemic problems beyond individual byte differences: (1) Our init opened with '0xFF {0x77,0x01,0x00,0x00,0x00}' then sent '0x13' as a standalone command. We intended 0x13 as a Command2 BK3 selector but the wire bits were the MIPI standard NORON (Normal Display On). Espressif opens with '0xFF {0x77,0x01,0x00,0x00,0x13}' — BK3 entered via the 0xFF parameter — then sends '0xEF {0x08}' in BK3. Our 0xEF landed in normal mode where the command has no effect. (2) The entire 0xE0..0xED GIP block differed. GIP values are what tell the gate drivers when to pulse each row; wrong values → rows that never activate → the mid-band stripe. Espressif's values are the known-good ones for the 480x480 Waveshare ST7701 family. Our 0xB0/0xB1 (BK0 positive/negative gamma) and the BK1 power-rail constants (0xB0 VOP 0x5D→0x8D, 0xB1 VCOM 0x2D→0x48, 0xB2 0x07→0x89, 0xB5 0x08→0x49, 0xB8 0x20→0x32) were also wrong, and an 0xEF 6-byte source-timing fine-trim block in BK1 was missing entirely. (3) Rounds 17 and 18 added a 0x3A COLMOD command (0x66 then 0x55) on the theory that pixel-format was wrong; espressif OMITS 0x3A entirely because the panel's power-on default pixel format is correct for its hardware strapping (IM[3:0] pins on the panel module select 16-bit RGB interface mode). Explicitly setting a non-default COLMOD silently misaligns bits on the RGB bus, which is consistent with the stripe pattern persisting across both 0x66 and 0x55 attempts. Round 19 drops the 0x3A addition. Also removed: the stray '{0x13, {}, 0, 0}' NORON send, the '0xB9 {0x10}' line that isn't in the reference. Also in st7701_panel.cpp: kCmdNoron constant deleted (no longer used), kCmdDispon post-delay changed from 50 ms to 0 ms per espressif. Only the init table changed this round — RGB timings, pin order, backlight, and TCA9554 reset sequence all stay exactly as round 18. If round 19 still stripes, the suspect shifts from 'software init' to 'RGB bus / timing' and round 20 should pivot to: (a) reversing data_gpio_nums pin order (some ESP-IDF 4.4.x builds put bit 0 on the LAST data_gpio_nums slot, not the first), (b) widening hsync_back_porch from 10 to 20 and reducing hsync_front_porch from 50 to 20 to match Espressif's typical 480x480 ST7701 timings, (c) dropping PCLK from 14 MHz to 10 MHz to rule out bus-bandwidth issues. Round 17 added the COLMOD command for the first time (rounds 13–16 had omitted it) and the stripe pattern's dominant colour shifted from 'mostly blue' in round 16 to 'more green and blue' in round 17 — evidence the panel IS responding to COLMOD, but 0x66 was the wrong value for our wiring. 0x66 is what espressif/esp-iot-solution's ST7701 driver uses, but espressif's reference board wires 18 data lines; Waveshare's ESP32-S3-Touch-LCD-2.1 only has 16 (B0..B4, G0..G5, R0..R4). When COLMOD=0x66 the ST7701 expects DB[17..12]=R, DB[11..6]=G, DB[5..0]=B; driving only DB[15..0] means the bit positions shift — our pixel's R MSB (bit 15) lands in the panel's R3 slot, R LSB (bit 11) lands in G5, G MSB (bit 10) lands in G4, etc. That cross-channel bit-shift is exactly the pattern that produces repeating-but-mis-coloured vertical stripes instead of coherent pixels. COLMOD=0x55 sets both the RGB (DPI) and MCU (DBI) interfaces to 16-bit 5-6-5 mode, which matches our 16 data lines exactly: DB[15..11]=R[4..0], DB[10..5]=G[5..0], DB[4..0]=B[4..0] — the natural RGB565 layout the ESP32 RGB peripheral puts on the wire with LV_COLOR_DEPTH=16 and LV_COLOR_16_SWAP=1. The ST7701S datasheet section 10.2.19 lists 0x55 as valid; LovyanGFX's config for Waveshare 16-line ST7701 boards uses it too. Single-byte change: in src/display/st7701_panel.cpp::kInitCmds[], {0x3A, {0x66}, 1, 0} becomes {0x3A, {0x55}, 1, 0}. The long-form comment above the entry now explains the 18bpp-vs-16bpp mismatch in full so the next developer doesn't flip it back to 0x66 chasing the espressif reference. Round 17 context preserved: that round also corrected 0xC0 display-line setting from 0x63 (800 lines) to 0x3B (480 lines) using the (NL+1)*8 formula — that fix stays in place since the 800-line mis-programming was independently wrong. If round 18 still shows stripes, remaining suspects in decreasing likelihood are: (a) horizontal timing — hsync_front_porch of 50 is unusually large vs Espressif's typical 20, widening the back porch at the expense of front porch could align the panel's sampling window (try hsync_pulse_width 10 / hsync_back_porch 20 / hsync_front_porch 20); (b) data_gpio_nums pin order — the ESP32 RGB peripheral might put bit 0 on DB[15] instead of DB[0] on some IDF versions, test by reversing the array; (c) COLMOD=0x50 as an alternative 16bpp value that some ST7701 revisions prefer over 0x55. Round 16 flipped PCLK polarity on the theory that round 15's stripes came from sampling data on the wrong clock edge; that hypothesis did not pan out (post-round-16 flash showed the same stripes, mostly blue hue). Re-reading our init table against espressif/esp-iot-solution's esp_lcd_st7701 driver and a handful of community ST7701 + Waveshare references surfaced two actual problems we had carried since round 13. (1) The init sequence never sends 0x3A. On power-up the ST7701 sits in whatever default pixel-format state its ROM leaves it in, which for RGB-interface operation is ambiguous across ST7701 revisions — some boot into a layout that pulls bits from our 16 data wires in a way that doesn't match RGB565. The mis-alignment between wire-level bits and the panel's internal pipeline bits is a textbook cause of the 'same data repeats as a vertical stripe with a dominant blue channel' pattern the monitor showed: when an RGB565 word (R5 G6 B5 = 16 bits) is read into an 18-bit RGB666 path without the panel being told it's in 18bpp mode, the B channel's LSBs land where G's MSBs would go, R's MSBs get truncated, and what survives is mostly the (large) low-bit blue values. Round 17 inserts {0x3A, {0x66}, 1, 0} — 18-bit RGB666 in RGB-interface mode — right after the 0xFF that exits Command2 vendor mode and before SLPOUT+DISPON. 0x66 is the value the espressif esp-iot-solution ST7701 driver uses, as does Waveshare's own vendor config; the alternative 0x55 (16bpp RGB565) is documented in the ST7701S datasheet but several revisions ship with it unsupported in RGB-interface mode, so 0x66 is the safer match. (2) 0xC0 Display Line Setting: byte 1 encodes (NL+1)*8 = number of display lines. 0x63 = 99, which programs the panel for (99+1)*8 = 800 lines. 480 lines requires NL = 59 = 0x3B, which is what round 17 sets. Driving a 480-line panel while it's internally gated for 800 lines smears rows across the physical array, which is also consistent with the 'middle 50% of the screen' framing in the stripe symptom. Both changes are in src/display/st7701_panel.cpp::kInitCmds[]: new 0x3A entry inserted, existing 0xC0 parameter changed from 0x63 to 0x3B. Long-form comments above both entries record the round-17 narrative so a future reader (likely us in round 20-something) doesn't undo the fix. Touch-controller side effect preserved from round 16: CST820 at 0x15 still ACKed-then-stopped after round 15's safe-state TCA9554 writes held TP_RST (bit 1) asserted low; not a v1 blocker because there's no touch code yet, but round 18+ will need to raise that bit before talking to the CST820. Historical context preserved from round 15: dark-screen fix moved backlight from TCA9554 to raw GPIO6 PWM (ledcSetup+ledcAttachPin+ledcWrite, 20 kHz, 10-bit, full duty) and shifted all TCA9554 bit-mask constants down by one (bit 0 = LCD_RST, bit 1 = TP_RST, bit 2 = LCD_CS, bit 7 = BUZZER) after realising the LGFX #630 EXIO1..EXIO8 labels are 1-indexed helper names mapping to P0..P7. Round 14 history preserved: removed cfg.bounce_buffer_size_px = 0 (that field was added in IDF 5.x; Arduino-ESP32 2.0.16 bundles IDF 4.4.7). Round 16 history preserved: pclk_active_neg 1→0 and vsync_pulse_width 8→2, vsync_front_porch 20→8 to align with FatihErtugral's ESP-IDF driver for the sibling Waveshare 2.8 inch ST7701 board. If round 17 still shows stripes, remaining suspects in decreasing likelihood are (a) RGB data-pin order reversed on one of R/G/B channels (LGFX #630 lists R0..R4, G0..G5, B0..B4 in ascending-bit order but some community repos use descending; swapping both channels' order independently is a cheap test), (b) horizontal timing porch values too tight for this panel sub-variant (try widening hsync_back_porch from 10 to 20 and hsync_front_porch from 50 to 30 to match espressif's defaults), (c) ST7701 init sequence has a gamma or GIP value that doesn't match this cell's glass (B0/B1/E5/E8 blocks).

(2) The entire 0xE0..0xED GIP block differed. GIP values are what tell the gate drivers when to pulse each row; wrong values → rows that never activate → the mid-band stripe. Espressif's values are the known-good ones for the 480x480 Waveshare ST7701 family. Our 0xB0/0xB1 (BK0 positive/negative gamma) and the BK1 power-rail constants (0xB0 VOP 0x5D→0x8D, 0xB1 VCOM 0x2D→0x48, 0xB2 0x07→0x89, 0xB5 0x08→0x49, 0xB8 0x20→0x32) were also wrong, and an 0xEF 6-byte source-timing fine-trim block in BK1 was missing entirely. (3) Rounds 17 and 18 added a 0x3A COLMOD command (0x66 then 0x55) on the theory that pixel-format was wrong; espressif OMITS 0x3A entirely because the panel's power-on default pixel format is correct for its hardware strapping (IM[3:0] pins on the panel module select 16-bit RGB interface mode). Explicitly setting a non-default COLMOD silently misaligns bits on the RGB bus, which is consistent with the stripe pattern persisting across both 0x66 and 0x55 attempts. Round 19 drops the 0x3A addition. Also removed: the stray '{0x13, {}, 0, 0}' NORON send, the '0xB9 {0x10}' line that isn't in the reference. Also in st7701_panel.cpp: kCmdNoron constant deleted (no longer used), kCmdDispon post-delay changed from 50 ms to 0 ms per espressif. Only the init table changed this round — RGB timings, pin order, backlight, and TCA9554 reset sequence all stay exactly as round 18. If round 19 still stripes, the suspect shifts from 'software init' to 'RGB bus / timing' and round 20 should pivot to: (a) reversing data_gpio_nums pin order (some ESP-IDF 4.4.x builds put bit 0 on the LAST data_gpio_nums slot, not the first), (b) widening hsync_back_porch from 10 to 20 and reducing hsync_front_porch from 50 to 20 to match Espressif's typical 480x480 ST7701 timings, (c) dropping PCLK from 14 MHz to 10 MHz to rule out bus-bandwidth issues. Round 17 added the COLMOD command for the first time (rounds 13–16 had omitted it) and the stripe pattern's dominant colour shifted from 'mostly blue' in round 16 to 'more green and blue' in round 17 — evidence the panel IS responding to COLMOD, but 0x66 was the wrong value for our wiring. 0x66 is what espressif/esp-iot-solution's ST7701 driver uses, but espressif's reference board wires 18 data lines; Waveshare's ESP32-S3-Touch-LCD-2.1 only has 16 (B0..B4, G0..G5, R0..R4). When COLMOD=0x66 the ST7701 expects DB[17..12]=R, DB[11..6]=G, DB[5..0]=B; driving only DB[15..0] means the bit positions shift — our pixel's R MSB (bit 15) lands in the panel's R3 slot, R LSB (bit 11) lands in G5, G MSB (bit 10) lands in G4, etc. That cross-channel bit-shift is exactly the pattern that produces repeating-but-mis-coloured vertical stripes instead of coherent pixels. COLMOD=0x55 sets both the RGB (DPI) and MCU (DBI) interfaces to 16-bit 5-6-5 mode, which matches our 16 data lines exactly: DB[15..11]=R[4..0], DB[10..5]=G[5..0], DB[4..0]=B[4..0] — the natural RGB565 layout the ESP32 RGB peripheral puts on the wire with LV_COLOR_DEPTH=16 and LV_COLOR_16_SWAP=1. The ST7701S datasheet section 10.2.19 lists 0x55 as valid; LovyanGFX's config for Waveshare 16-line ST7701 boards uses it too. Single-byte change: in src/display/st7701_panel.cpp::kInitCmds[], {0x3A, {0x66}, 1, 0} becomes {0x3A, {0x55}, 1, 0}. The long-form comment above the entry now explains the 18bpp-vs-16bpp mismatch in full so the next developer doesn't flip it back to 0x66 chasing the espressif reference. Round 17 context preserved: that round also corrected 0xC0 display-line setting from 0x63 (800 lines) to 0x3B (480 lines) using the (NL+1)*8 formula — that fix stays in place since the 800-line mis-programming was independently wrong. If round 18 still shows stripes, remaining suspects in decreasing likelihood are: (a) horizontal timing — hsync_front_porch of 50 is unusually large vs Espressif's typical 20, widening the back porch at the expense of front porch could align the panel's sampling window (try hsync_pulse_width 10 / hsync_back_porch 20 / hsync_front_porch 20); (b) data_gpio_nums pin order — the ESP32 RGB peripheral might put bit 0 on DB[15] instead of DB[0] on some IDF versions, test by reversing the array; (c) COLMOD=0x50 as an alternative 16bpp value that some ST7701 revisions prefer over 0x55. Round 16 flipped PCLK polarity on the theory that round 15's stripes came from sampling data on the wrong clock edge; that hypothesis did not pan out (post-round-16 flash showed the same stripes, mostly blue hue). Re-reading our init table against espressif/esp-iot-solution's esp_lcd_st7701 driver and a handful of community ST7701 + Waveshare references surfaced two actual problems we had carried since round 13. (1) The init sequence never sends 0x3A. On power-up the ST7701 sits in whatever default pixel-format state its ROM leaves it in, which for RGB-interface operation is ambiguous across ST7701 revisions — some boot into a layout that pulls bits from our 16 data wires in a way that doesn't match RGB565. The mis-alignment between wire-level bits and the panel's internal pipeline bits is a textbook cause of the 'same data repeats as a vertical stripe with a dominant blue channel' pattern the monitor showed: when an RGB565 word (R5 G6 B5 = 16 bits) is read into an 18-bit RGB666 path without the panel being told it's in 18bpp mode, the B channel's LSBs land where G's MSBs would go, R's MSBs get truncated, and what survives is mostly the (large) low-bit blue values. Round 17 inserts {0x3A, {0x66}, 1, 0} — 18-bit RGB666 in RGB-interface mode — right after the 0xFF that exits Command2 vendor mode and before SLPOUT+DISPON. 0x66 is the value the espressif esp-iot-solution ST7701 driver uses, as does Waveshare's own vendor config; the alternative 0x55 (16bpp RGB565) is documented in the ST7701S datasheet but several revisions ship with it unsupported in RGB-interface mode, so 0x66 is the safer match. (2) 0xC0 Display Line Setting: byte 1 encodes (NL+1)*8 = number of display lines. 0x63 = 99, which programs the panel for (99+1)*8 = 800 lines. 480 lines requires NL = 59 = 0x3B, which is what round 17 sets. Driving a 480-line panel while it's internally gated for 800 lines smears rows across the physical array, which is also consistent with the 'middle 50% of the screen' framing in the stripe symptom. Both changes are in src/display/st7701_panel.cpp::kInitCmds[]: new 0x3A entry inserted, existing 0xC0 parameter changed from 0x63 to 0x3B. Long-form comments above both entries record the round-17 narrative so a future reader (likely us in round 20-something) doesn't undo the fix. Touch-controller side effect preserved from round 16: CST820 at 0x15 still ACKed-then-stopped after round 15's safe-state TCA9554 writes held TP_RST (bit 1) asserted low; not a v1 blocker because there's no touch code yet, but round 18+ will need to raise that bit before talking to the CST820. Historical context preserved from round 15: dark-screen fix moved backlight from TCA9554 to raw GPIO6 PWM (ledcSetup+ledcAttachPin+ledcWrite, 20 kHz, 10-bit, full duty) and shifted all TCA9554 bit-mask constants down by one (bit 0 = LCD_RST, bit 1 = TP_RST, bit 2 = LCD_CS, bit 7 = BUZZER) after realising the LGFX #630 EXIO1..EXIO8 labels are 1-indexed helper names mapping to P0..P7. Round 14 history preserved: removed cfg.bounce_buffer_size_px = 0 (that field was added in IDF 5.x; Arduino-ESP32 2.0.16 bundles IDF 4.4.7). Round 16 history preserved: pclk_active_neg 1→0 and vsync_pulse_width 8→2, vsync_front_porch 20→8 to align with FatihErtugral's ESP-IDF driver for the sibling Waveshare 2.8 inch ST7701 board. If round 17 still shows stripes, remaining suspects in decreasing likelihood are (a) RGB data-pin order reversed on one of R/G/B channels (LGFX #630 lists R0..R4, G0..G5, B0..B4 in ascending-bit order but some community repos use descending; swapping both channels' order independently is a cheap test), (b) horizontal timing porch values too tight for this panel sub-variant (try widening hsync_back_porch from 10 to 20 and hsync_front_porch from 50 to 30 to match espressif's defaults), (c) ST7701 init sequence has a gamma or GIP value that doesn't match this cell's glass (B0/B1/E5/E8 blocks).
- **2026-04-24** — Display bring-up round 20: pivot from init-sequence edits to RGB-bus timing. Round 19 shipped a verbatim port of espressif's ST7701 init sequence and the display output did not change from round 18 — same uniform-blue background, same column of green+blue stripes compressed into the middle ~1/3 of the screen. The fact that a completely different init sequence produced an identical visual symptom is diagnostic: the problem is not in what commands we send to the panel, it is in HOW we drive the 16 RGB data lines and their sync/porch signals afterward. Round 20 retunes the RGB peripheral in two parts. (a) PCLK drops from 14 MHz to 10 MHz in display_pins.h::RGB_PCLK_HZ. Rounds 14–19 used 14 MHz because that's what FatihErtugral's working config for the sibling Waveshare 2.8" ST7701 board ships; but on our 2.1" 480×480 panel 14 MHz is apparently outrunning the source-driver sampling window given our generous front porch. 10 MHz is well inside the ST7701S-datasheet-guaranteed band (~3 MHz to ~20 MHz) and biases for 'works' over 'max refresh'. We can step back up to 12–14 MHz once the image is coherent. (b) Porches move from FatihErtugral's values to Espressif's Waveshare-BSP typical values. Specifically: hsync_pulse_width 8→10, hsync_back_porch 10→20, hsync_front_porch 50→20, vsync_pulse_width 2→10, vsync_back_porch 18→10, vsync_front_porch 8→10 in st7701_panel.cpp::initRgbPanel(). The single largest delta is hsync_front_porch dropping from 50 to 20 — 50 was ~5x the value Espressif uses for comparable 480×480 ST7701 BSPs and is the strongest suspect for why the panel's HSYNC resync arrives too late per line, with pixels at the end of one line bleeding into the start of the next. The new porch+PCLK combo gives total 530×510 clocks per frame @ 10 MHz = 37 Hz refresh (down from 50 Hz); flickery on a bench but harmless for bring-up. Init sequence is untouched from round 19 (verbatim espressif port). Pin order, backlight, and TCA9554 reset sequence all unchanged. If round 20 visibly changes the stripe pattern — width, shape, or position — timing was involved and round 21 can fine-tune from there. If round 20 shows no change at all (same as rounds 18/19), timing is not the issue and the suspect shifts to pin order or LV_COLOR_16_SWAP polarity; round 21 would then reverse data_gpio_nums to test whether the ESP-IDF 4.4.7 RGB peripheral puts bit 0 on the last array slot rather than the first. Historical context preserved from round 19: that round replaced our round-13 init table (stitched from Nicolai-Electronics + generic ST7701S datasheet) with a verbatim port of espressif/esp-iot-solution/esp_lcd_st7701_rgb.c::vendor_specific_init_default[]. Key fixes in that port were (1) BK3 entry via 0xFF {...,0x13} instead of a stray MIPI NORON, (2) entire 0xE0..0xED GIP block replaced with espressif's known-good values, (3) dropped the 0x3A COLMOD addition from rounds 17/18. None of those changes moved the visual symptom, which is what triggered the round-20 pivot. Round 18's photo showed a uniform blue background with a vertical column of green+blue stripes spanning the middle ~1/3 of the screen — a textbook gate-in-panel (GIP) timing mismatch where most columns of the panel's source drivers never get the right gate pulse and stay in their power-on blue state, while a narrow band actually scans the data we send. Rounds 13–18 used an init table stitched together from Nicolai-Electronics/esp32-component-st7701 + the generic ST7701S datasheet sequence; cross-checking that table against espressif's known-good sequence (pulled from the current master of esp-iot-solution's esp_lcd_st7701 driver) surfaced three systemic problems beyond individual byte differences: (1) Our init opened with '0xFF {0x77,0x01,0x00,0x00,0x00}' then sent '0x13' as a standalone command. We intended 0x13 as a Command2 BK3 selector but the wire bits were the MIPI standard NORON (Normal Display On). Espressif opens with '0xFF {0x77,0x01,0x00,0x00,0x13}' — BK3 entered via the 0xFF parameter — then sends '0xEF {0x08}' in BK3. Our 0xEF landed in normal mode where the command has no effect. (2) The entire 0xE0..0xED GIP block differed. GIP values are what tell the gate drivers when to pulse each row; wrong values → rows that never activate → the mid-band stripe. Espressif's values are the known-good ones for the 480x480 Waveshare ST7701 family. Our 0xB0/0xB1 (BK0 positive/negative gamma) and the BK1 power-rail constants (0xB0 VOP 0x5D→0x8D, 0xB1 VCOM 0x2D→0x48, 0xB2 0x07→0x89, 0xB5 0x08→0x49, 0xB8 0x20→0x32) were also wrong, and an 0xEF 6-byte source-timing fine-trim block in BK1 was missing entirely. (3) Rounds 17 and 18 added a 0x3A COLMOD command (0x66 then 0x55) on the theory that pixel-format was wrong; espressif OMITS 0x3A entirely because the panel's power-on default pixel format is correct for its hardware strapping (IM[3:0] pins on the panel module select 16-bit RGB interface mode). Explicitly setting a non-default COLMOD silently misaligns bits on the RGB bus, which is consistent with the stripe pattern persisting across both 0x66 and 0x55 attempts. Round 19 drops the 0x3A addition. Also removed: the stray '{0x13, {}, 0, 0}' NORON send, the '0xB9 {0x10}' line that isn't in the reference. Also in st7701_panel.cpp: kCmdNoron constant deleted (no longer used), kCmdDispon post-delay changed from 50 ms to 0 ms per espressif. Only the init table changed this round — RGB timings, pin order, backlight, and TCA9554 reset sequence all stay exactly as round 18. If round 19 still stripes, the suspect shifts from 'software init' to 'RGB bus / timing' and round 20 should pivot to: (a) reversing data_gpio_nums pin order (some ESP-IDF 4.4.x builds put bit 0 on the LAST data_gpio_nums slot, not the first), (b) widening hsync_back_porch from 10 to 20 and reducing hsync_front_porch from 50 to 20 to match Espressif's typical 480x480 ST7701 timings, (c) dropping PCLK from 14 MHz to 10 MHz to rule out bus-bandwidth issues. Round 17 added the COLMOD command for the first time (rounds 13–16 had omitted it) and the stripe pattern's dominant colour shifted from 'mostly blue' in round 16 to 'more green and blue' in round 17 — evidence the panel IS responding to COLMOD, but 0x66 was the wrong value for our wiring. 0x66 is what espressif/esp-iot-solution's ST7701 driver uses, but espressif's reference board wires 18 data lines; Waveshare's ESP32-S3-Touch-LCD-2.1 only has 16 (B0..B4, G0..G5, R0..R4). When COLMOD=0x66 the ST7701 expects DB[17..12]=R, DB[11..6]=G, DB[5..0]=B; driving only DB[15..0] means the bit positions shift — our pixel's R MSB (bit 15) lands in the panel's R3 slot, R LSB (bit 11) lands in G5, G MSB (bit 10) lands in G4, etc. That cross-channel bit-shift is exactly the pattern that produces repeating-but-mis-coloured vertical stripes instead of coherent pixels. The ST7701S datasheet section 10.2.19 lists 0x55 as valid; LovyanGFX's config for Waveshare 16-line ST7701 boards uses it too. Single-byte change: in src/display/st7701_panel.cpp::kInitCmds[], {0x3A, {0x66}, 1, 0} becomes {0x3A, {0x55}, 1, 0}. The long-form comment above the entry now explains the 18bpp-vs-16bpp mismatch in full so the next developer doesn't flip it back to 0x66 chasing the espressif reference. Round 17 context preserved: that round also corrected 0xC0 display-line setting from 0x63 (800 lines) to 0x3B (480 lines) using the (NL+1)*8 formula — that fix stays in place since the 800-line mis-programming was independently wrong. On power-up the ST7701 sits in whatever default pixel-format state its ROM leaves it in, which for RGB-interface operation is ambiguous across ST7701 revisions — some boot into a layout that pulls bits from our 16 data wires in a way that doesn't match RGB565. The mis-alignment between wire-level bits and the panel's internal pipeline bits is a textbook cause of the 'same data repeats as a vertical stripe with a dominant blue channel' pattern the monitor showed: when an RGB565 word (R5 G6 B5 = 16 bits) is read into an 18-bit RGB666 path without the panel being told it's in 18bpp mode, the B channel's LSBs land where G's MSBs would go, R's MSBs get truncated, and what survives is mostly the (large) low-bit blue values. Round 17 inserts {0x3A, {0x66}, 1, 0} — 18-bit RGB666 in RGB-interface mode — right after the 0xFF that exits Command2 vendor mode and before SLPOUT+DISPON. 0x66 is the value the espressif esp-iot-solution ST7701 driver uses, as does Waveshare's own vendor config; the alternative 0x55 (16bpp RGB565) is documented in the ST7701S datasheet but several revisions ship with it unsupported in RGB-interface mode, so 0x66 is the safer match. (2) 0xC0 Display Line Setting: byte 1 encodes (NL+1)*8 = number of display lines. 0x63 = 99, which programs the panel for (99+1)*8 = 800 lines. 480 lines requires NL = 59 = 0x3B, which is what round 17 sets. Driving a 480-line panel while it's internally gated for 800 lines smears rows across the physical array, which is also consistent with the 'middle 50% of the screen' framing in the stripe symptom. Both changes are in src/display/st7701_panel.cpp::kInitCmds[]: new 0x3A entry inserted, existing 0xC0 parameter changed from 0x63 to 0x3B. Long-form comments above both entries record the round-17 narrative so a future reader (likely us in round 20-something) doesn't undo the fix. Touch-controller side effect preserved from round 16: CST820 at 0x15 still ACKed-then-stopped after round 15's safe-state TCA9554 writes held TP_RST (bit 1) asserted low; not a v1 blocker because there's no touch code yet, but round 18+ will need to raise that bit before talking to the CST820. Historical context preserved from round 15: dark-screen fix moved backlight from TCA9554 to raw GPIO6 PWM (ledcSetup+ledcAttachPin+ledcWrite, 20 kHz, 10-bit, full duty) and shifted all TCA9554 bit-mask constants down by one (bit 0 = LCD_RST, bit 1 = TP_RST, bit 2 = LCD_CS, bit 7 = BUZZER) after realising the LGFX #630 EXIO1..EXIO8 labels are 1-indexed helper names mapping to P0..P7. Round 14 history preserved: removed cfg.bounce_buffer_size_px = 0 (that field was added in IDF 5.x; Arduino-ESP32 2.0.16 bundles IDF 4.4.7). Round 16 history preserved: pclk_active_neg 1→0 and vsync_pulse_width 8→2, vsync_front_porch 20→8 to align with FatihErtugral's ESP-IDF driver for the sibling Waveshare 2.8 inch ST7701 board. If round 17 still shows stripes, remaining suspects in decreasing likelihood are (a) RGB data-pin order reversed on one of R/G/B channels (LGFX #630 lists R0..R4, G0..G5, B0..B4 in ascending-bit order but some community repos use descending; swapping both channels' order independently is a cheap test), (b) horizontal timing porch values too tight for this panel sub-variant (try widening hsync_back_porch from 10 to 20 and hsync_front_porch from 50 to 30 to match espressif's defaults), (c) ST7701 init sequence has a gamma or GIP value that doesn't match this cell's glass (B0/B1/E5/E8 blocks).
- **2026-04-23** — Display bring-up round 18: correct the COLMOD (0x3A) parameter from 0x66 (18-bit RGB666) to 0x55 (16-bit RGB565) so the panel's expected data-bit layout matches our actual 16-line RGB bus. Round 17 added the COLMOD command for the first time (rounds 13–16 had omitted it) and the stripe pattern's dominant colour shifted from 'mostly blue' in round 16 to 'more green and blue' in round 17 — evidence the panel IS responding to COLMOD, but 0x66 was the wrong value for our wiring. 0x66 is what espressif/esp-iot-solution's ST7701 driver uses, but espressif's reference board wires 18 data lines; Waveshare's ESP32-S3-Touch-LCD-2.1 only has 16 (B0..B4, G0..G5, R0..R4). When COLMOD=0x66 the ST7701 expects DB[17..12]=R, DB[11..6]=G, DB[5..0]=B; driving only DB[15..0] means the bit positions shift — our pixel's R MSB (bit 15) lands in the panel's R3 slot, R LSB (bit 11) lands in G5, G MSB (bit 10) lands in G4, etc. That cross-channel bit-shift is exactly the pattern that produces repeating-but-mis-coloured vertical stripes instead of coherent pixels. COLMOD=0x55 sets both the RGB (DPI) and MCU (DBI) interfaces to 16-bit 5-6-5 mode, which matches our 16 data lines exactly: DB[15..11]=R[4..0], DB[10..5]=G[5..0], DB[4..0]=B[4..0] — the natural RGB565 layout the ESP32 RGB peripheral puts on the wire with LV_COLOR_DEPTH=16 and LV_COLOR_16_SWAP=1. The ST7701S datasheet section 10.2.19 lists 0x55 as valid; LovyanGFX's config for Waveshare 16-line ST7701 boards uses it too. Single-byte change: in src/display/st7701_panel.cpp::kInitCmds[], {0x3A, {0x66}, 1, 0} becomes {0x3A, {0x55}, 1, 0}. The long-form comment above the entry now explains the 18bpp-vs-16bpp mismatch in full so the next developer doesn't flip it back to 0x66 chasing the espressif reference. Round 17 context preserved: that round also corrected 0xC0 display-line setting from 0x63 (800 lines) to 0x3B (480 lines) using the (NL+1)*8 formula — that fix stays in place since the 800-line mis-programming was independently wrong. If round 18 still shows stripes, remaining suspects in decreasing likelihood are: (a) horizontal timing — hsync_front_porch of 50 is unusually large vs Espressif's typical 20, widening the back porch at the expense of front porch could align the panel's sampling window (try hsync_pulse_width 10 / hsync_back_porch 20 / hsync_front_porch 20); (b) data_gpio_nums pin order — the ESP32 RGB peripheral might put bit 0 on DB[15] instead of DB[0] on some IDF versions, test by reversing the array; (c) COLMOD=0x50 as an alternative 16bpp value that some ST7701 revisions prefer over 0x55. Round 16 flipped PCLK polarity on the theory that round 15's stripes came from sampling data on the wrong clock edge; that hypothesis did not pan out (post-round-16 flash showed the same stripes, mostly blue hue). Re-reading our init table against espressif/esp-iot-solution's esp_lcd_st7701 driver and a handful of community ST7701 + Waveshare references surfaced two actual problems we had carried since round 13. (1) The init sequence never sends 0x3A. On power-up the ST7701 sits in whatever default pixel-format state its ROM leaves it in, which for RGB-interface operation is ambiguous across ST7701 revisions — some boot into a layout that pulls bits from our 16 data wires in a way that doesn't match RGB565. The mis-alignment between wire-level bits and the panel's internal pipeline bits is a textbook cause of the 'same data repeats as a vertical stripe with a dominant blue channel' pattern the monitor showed: when an RGB565 word (R5 G6 B5 = 16 bits) is read into an 18-bit RGB666 path without the panel being told it's in 18bpp mode, the B channel's LSBs land where G's MSBs would go, R's MSBs get truncated, and what survives is mostly the (large) low-bit blue values. (2) 0xC0 Display Line Setting: byte 1 encodes (NL+1)*8 = number of display lines. 0x63 = 99, which programs the panel for (99+1)*8 = 800 lines. 480 lines requires NL = 59 = 0x3B, which is what round 17 sets. Driving a 480-line panel while it's internally gated for 800 lines smears rows across the physical array, which is also consistent with the 'middle 50% of the screen' framing in the stripe symptom. Long-form comments above both entries record the round-17 narrative so a future reader (likely us in round 20-something) doesn't undo the fix. - **2026-04-23** — Display bring-up round 15: fix the two wrong assumptions that kept the round-14 driver producing a black screen. Round 14 compiled clean, flashed fine, and every log line reported success — TCA9554 acked, 37-command ST7701 init sequence sent, esp_lcd_new_rgb_panel up at 14 MHz PCLK with a 480x480 PSRAM framebuffer, backlight bit set, LVGL alive — but the panel still showed nothing. A second read of the LovyanGFX discussion #630 config for this exact board (the same source we used for the RGB pin map) surfaced two off-by-one errors we'd been carrying since round 13. First: the backlight is not on the TCA9554 at all. It lives on RAW GPIO6 with PWM via Waveshare's ledcAttach(6, 20000, 10). Our own boot-log GPIO idle-state scan showed gpio 6 sitting LOW with nothing driving it, which is exactly what an unpowered backlight FET gate looks like — the clue was in our own logs, we just didn't know what to do with it. Second: the TCA9554 EXIO labels in the LGFX config are 1-indexed helper names, not direct bit numbers: EXIO1 is bit 0, EXIO2 is bit 1, EXIO3 is bit 2, EXIO8 is bit 7. Round 13 read them as direct bit numbers which shifted every signal up by one, so round 14's panel-reset pulse was actually hitting the touch-reset line and the ST7701 was never reset. It stayed in its power-on idle state and ignored the init sequence entirely, which explains both the dark screen and why the backlight bit we were toggling (TCA9554 IO0 = actually LCD_RST) made no visible difference. Round 15 fixes are all in display_pins.h and st7701_panel.cpp: the TCA9554 bit-mask constants shift down by one (bit 0 = LCD_RST, bit 1 = TP_RST, bit 2 = LCD_CS, bit 7 = BUZZER untouched because bit 7 is bit 7 either way which is the accidental reason round-12 beep detection produced the right buzzer mapping), TCA9554_BIT_LCD_BL is deleted entirely, new BACKLIGHT_PIN / BACKLIGHT_PWM_CH / BACKLIGHT_PWM_FREQ / BACKLIGHT_PWM_RES / BACKLIGHT_PWM_FULL constants describe the GPIO6 PWM setup, and St7701Panel::begin() replaces the TCA9554 backlight-enable call with ledcSetup(0, 20000, 10) + ledcAttachPin(6, 0) + ledcWrite(0, 1023). Arduino-ESP32 2.0.16 doesn't have the ledcAttach convenience API (that's 3.x) so we use the 3-function form. WIRING.md display and TCA9554 tables are regenerated with the corrected mapping, tca9554.cpp safe-state comment matches, and the display_pins.h header gains a round-15 pivot note that explains the mistake in full so future readers don't undo it. Next flash should paint the LVGL boot screen; if it's still dark, the remaining suspects in decreasing likelihood are (a) RGB timing porch values off, resolvable by widening h_back_porch / v_back_porch, (b) wrong ST7701 init sequence for this specific panel sub-variant, (c) RGB data-pin order wrong on one of R/G/B (would show as correct brightness but garbled colour, not black, so unlikely).
- **2026-04-23** — Display bring-up round 15: fix the two wrong assumptions that kept the round-14 driver producing a black screen. Round 14 compiled clean, flashed fine, and every log line reported success — TCA9554 acked, 37-command ST7701 init sequence sent, esp_lcd_new_rgb_panel up at 14 MHz PCLK with a 480x480 PSRAM framebuffer, backlight bit set, LVGL alive — but the panel still showed nothing. - **2026-04-23** — Display bring-up round 14: ship the real ST7701 RGB driver and retire the ST77916 QSPI stub. Round 13 established the chipset pivot on paper; round 14 turns that into running code. New files src/display/st7701_panel.h and st7701_panel.cpp implement the panel against ESP-IDF's esp_lcd_panel_rgb, which ships inside the Arduino-ESP32 2.0.16 IDF 4.4.7 fork so no toolchain bump is needed. Bring-up runs in six steps inside begin(): assert LCD_RST through TCA9554 IO1, release it and wait 120 ms for the ST7701 PLL, bit-bang the 37-command vendor init sequence over a 3-wire SPI link built from SCK=GPIO2 + SDA=GPIO1 + CS=TCA9554 IO3 using 9-bit transactions (one DCX bit then 8 data bits MSB-first), construct esp_lcd_new_rgb_panel with the full 16-bit RGB pin map and porch timings from display_pins.h at 14 MHz PCLK with a PSRAM-backed 480x480x2 framebuffer, call esp_lcd_panel_init to push the first frame and start PCLK, then raise LCD_BL on TCA9554 IO0 last so the first visible state is a blacked-out framebuffer rather than DRAM garbage. The init table is sourced from Nicolai-Electronics/esp32-component-st7701 vendor_specific_init_default[] — same BK0/BK1 gamma + GIP sequence that the Waveshare reference demo uses, just spelled out as a C array instead of hidden inside a vendor LCD_Driver component. drawBitmap() and fillColor() are thin wrappers over esp_lcd_panel_draw_bitmap so Ui.cpp's flush_cb keeps the identical signature it had for ST77916 — the only line that changed in Ui.cpp is the #include and class type swap from display::St77916Panel to display::St7701Panel plus a log-message update. st77916_panel.h and st77916_panel.cpp are deleted. If PSRAM framebuffer allocation fails (8 MB board but a runaway task could still exhaust it) begin() returns false and the LVGL flush becomes a no-op rather than crashing. First compile attempt also flagged a struct-field mismatch: cfg.bounce_buffer_size_px does not exist in IDF 4.4.7 — that field was added in IDF 5.x as part of the SRAM bounce-buffer fast path for high-PCLK PSRAM framebuffers. At 14 MHz we don't need it anyway, so the line is removed and replaced with a comment pointing at the IDF version pivot for future reference. Next flash should paint the LVGL boot screen; if it's still dark, suspects are: (a) IO0=LCD_BL hypothesis, verifiable by driving that bit high in isolation, (b) SPI init pins GPIO1/GPIO2 wrong on this board revision, verifiable by checking factory firmware pin usage, (c) timing porch values mismatched, resolvable by widening h_back_porch / v_back_porch.
- **2026-04-23** — Display bring-up round 13: reframe after factory-firmware evidence, capture the real ST7701 RGB pinout. User reported that when they first powered the board over USB-C, before any of our firmware was flashed, the factory demo image displayed a working settings UI on the screen. That is conclusive proof that the panel, backlight, touch, and every supporting rail on this board are fully functional, and our dark screen is pure driver-protocol mismatch: an ST77916 QSPI init sequence sent to an ST7701 RGB panel renders as zero pixels, and without valid pixel data the LC layer stays opaque, which is also why the round-12 TCA9554 bit-walk never lit any phase visibly. Round 13 captures everything we just learned. display_pins.h gains a full RGB parallel-bus section: HSYNC=38, VSYNC=39, DE=40, PCLK=41 at 14 MHz, plus 16 RGB565 data lines on 46,3,8,18,17 / 14,13,12,11,10,9 / 5,45,48,47,21, all sourced from LovyanGFX discussion 630 for this exact board and cross-checked against the Waveshare product page. TCA9554 bit mapping gets corrected too: IO1=LCD_RST, IO2=TP_RST, IO3=LCD_CS for the panel 3-wire-SPI init bus. Rounds 11-12 had IO1 and IO2 swapped, and had IO3 labelled SD_CS which is wrong for this variant. IO7 is recorded as a piezo buzzer active high from the round-12 phase-B and phase-J beeps. IO4-IO6 stay unassigned until we find something. Ui.cpp loses the round-12 bit-mapping diagnostic block which wasted roughly 20 s per boot and cannot teach us anything further. WIRING.md replaces its display pinout table with the ST7701 RGB target table plus a legacy ST77916 QSPI table kept only as a record of what the stub driver is still wired to. No new panel code this round; actually writing src/display/st7701_panel.{h,cpp} with esp_lcd_panel_rgb and a 480x480x2 PSRAM framebuffer is round 14. tca9554.cpp also gets a comment refresh so the safe-state notes match the new mapping.
- **2026-04-23** — Display bring-up round 12: TCA9554 IO-to-signal mapping diagnostic. Round 11 landed cleanly (TCA9554 ACK at 0x20, config+output writes accepted) but the backlight still never came on, which means our guess IO0=LCD_BL active-high is wrong for this board rev. Rather than guess again, brute-force it. New diagnostic block in src/Ui.cpp runs right after TCA9554.begin and before ST77916.begin stomps state: 10 phases, each held 2 s, logged with a distinctive phase letter. Phase A = all bits LOW, phase B = all bits HIGH, phases C..J = one bit HIGH walking IO0..IO7. Operator watches the screen and reports which phase letter(s) light the backlight. Decoding chart in the block comment: phase B plus one C..J means active-HIGH on that bit; phase A plus every C..J except one means active-LOW on the missing bit's letter; nothing at all means the backlight isn't wired through TCA9554 and round 13 pivots to a direct-GPIO probe. No bit mapping changed yet; display_pins.h's TCA9554_BIT_* constants stay as-is until we have the reported phase letter. Diagnostic adds ~20 s to boot; removed once we know the answer.
- **2026-04-23** — Display bring-up round 11: port expander driver from CH422G to TCA9554 and update every callsite / doc to match the pivot. Round 10's log produced two payoffs: (a) SDA=GPIO15 is locked, and (b) SCL=GPIO7 is locked indirectly — every SCL candidate produced the same 5-device ACK set (0x15, 0x20, 0x51, 0x6B, 0x7E), which is a known Arduino-ESP32 quirk where Wire.end() releases the driver but not the GPIO matrix routing, so the *first* successful begin (SCL=7) physically drove the bus for every subsequent iteration. The real bus fingerprint is five devices: CST820 touch, TCA9554 expander, PCF85063 RTC, probably a QMI8658 IMU at 0x6B, and an unknown/spurious thing at 0x7E. This round lands the driver work that round 10 only *documented*: (1) new src/display/tca9554.{h,cpp} implementing class Tca9554 with the standard register-pointer protocol (write reg 0x03 = 0x00 to make all 8 IOs outputs, then write reg 0x01 to drive them); public API (begin/writeOutput/setBits/clearBits/shadow) is deliberately identical to the old Ch422g class so the panel code swaps without ceremony. (2) Deleted src/display/ch422g.{h,cpp}. (3) st77916_panel.{h,cpp} now takes a Tca9554& instead of a Ch422g&, references TCA9554_BIT_LCD_BL / TCA9554_BIT_LCD_RST. (4) Ui.cpp now declares 'display::Tca9554 g_expander', includes display/tca9554.h, logs 'TCA9554.begin()' instead of 'CH422G.begin()', and its comment header is rewritten to state plainly that the board is the ST7701+TCA9554 variant (kept the ST77916 driver for now; round 12 rips it out). (5) Replaced round 10's 420-pair SCL-verification block with a single 127-address boot-time bus enumeration on the locked SDA=15/SCL=7 pair — still prints every ACKed address so we can see at a glance whether the bus came up with the expected five devices. (6) display_pins.h: CH422G_* symbols deleted, TCA9554_* symbols (addr 0x20, reg 0x03 CONFIG, reg 0x01 OUTPUT, bits IO0=LCD_BL / IO1=TP_RST / IO2=LCD_RST / IO3=SD_CS) made primary, pivot-plan updated, 0x6B/0x7E documented as best-guess IMU + unknown. (7) docs/WIRING.md rewritten to reflect the pivot (TCA9554 table, updated SDA/SCL to 15/7). Expected round-11 boot log: I2C bus enumeration shows ACKs at 0x15/0x20/0x51/0x6B/0x7E, then 'tca9554 ok (addr=0x20, config=0x00, output=0x00)' where round 10 got 'ch422g mode-register write to 0x24 NACKed'. The ST77916 block will still claim success while driving nothing — that's round 12's problem.
- **2026-04-23** — Display bring-up round 10: CHIPSET PIVOT. Round 9's exhaustive 420-pair I2C scan produced a clean result — only SDA=GPIO15 ever ACKs, and the only three addresses that respond are 0x15 (CST820 touch), 0x20 (TCA9554 I/O expander), and 0x51 (PCF85063 RTC). 0x24 and 0x38 — the CH422G MODE + WR_IO registers — never ACKed on any pin pair, meaning the board does NOT host a CH422G at all. That address signature (0x15 / 0x20 / 0x51) matches Waveshare's *other* 'ESP32-S3-Touch-LCD-2.1' BOM: ST7701 RGB panel (NOT QSPI ST77916) + TCA9554 expander (NOT CH422G) + CST820 + PCF85063. Every one of our last 9 rounds has been building drivers for the wrong chipset family. This round does the minimum useful thing with that information: (1) lock I2C pins in display_pins.h to SDA=GPIO15 / SCL=GPIO7 (GPIO7 is Waveshare's silkscreen convention on the 4' sibling board; it gets verified at boot), (2) document the chipset pivot inline with a pivot plan (round 11 = swap ch422g.cpp for TCA9554; round 12+ = replace ST77916 QSPI driver with esp_lcd_panel_rgb ST7701 + PSRAM framebuffer), (3) add TCA9554 register/bit definitions (TCA9554_REG_CONFIG=0x03, TCA9554_REG_OUTPUT=0x01, bits IO0=LCD_BL / IO1=TP_RST / IO2=LCD_RST / IO3=SD_CS) alongside the existing CH422G ones — the CH422G symbols stay temporarily so ch422g.cpp still links, but are clearly marked UNUSED, (4) swap round 9's 420-pair exhaustive scan for a targeted round-10 diagnostic that fixes SDA=GPIO15 and runs the full 127-address scan on each SCL candidate in {7, 1, 2, 5, 8, 9, 16}. The correct SCL will produce exactly three ACKs (0x15 / 0x20 / 0x51); wrong SCLs will drop ACKs or produce spurious ones. Once round 10's serial log confirms SCL=GPIO7 gives the clean 3-hit set, round 11 can rip out ch422g.cpp and move on to the ST7701 RGB rewrite. No driver code changes this round — purely diagnostic + pivot documentation.
- **2026-04-22** — Display bring-up round 6: I2C is still blind on GPIO8/9 (both orderings) AND GPIO10/11 (both orderings) — we've exhausted the plausible guesses derived from other Waveshare CH422G boards. Stop guessing, start diagnosing: add a probeIdle() in Ui.cpp::begin() that, BEFORE Wire.begin(), drives pins as INPUT_PULLUP, waits 200 µs, and reads them. Both HIGH = bus electrically healthy (wrong pins or dead device). Either LOW = bus shorted / missing 3V3 / stuck peripheral — in which case no amount of pin guessing will help. We probe three candidate pairs in one flash (8/9, 10/11, 6/7) so one serial dump tells us which GPIOs even look like a live I2C bus on this particular board. SPI/QSPI side still unchanged — SPI3_HOST, 64-byte sendPixels chunking, minimal init sequence. Expectation for this flash: the idle-state log narrows 'pin problem' vs 'electrical problem' so we know whether to keep trying pins or pull out a multimeter.
- **2026-04-22** — Display bring-up round 4: SPI side now clean — 64-byte sendPixels chunking, SPI3_HOST, and dropping spi_bus_free made runInitSequence/backlight-on/fillColor go through with no 'txdata transfer > hardware max supported len' errors on the panel. I2C side still blind: scan sees zero devices at 100 kHz with pins (SDA=11, SCL=10). That leaves pin-swap as the strongest remaining candidate — Waveshare has shipped multiple ESP32-S3-Touch-LCD-2.1 revisions with SDA/SCL swapped. So Ui.cpp::begin() now tries the documented pin order first, scans; if zero devices, calls Wire.end() and re-inits with pins swapped, scans again. Whichever ordering ACKs devices is the one we keep. Also moved the scan out of Ch422g::begin() (now run once in Ui.cpp before the expander is touched) and dropped I2C to 100 kHz to tolerate the ESP32's weak internal pull-ups in case there are no board-level pull-ups.
- **2026-04-22** — Real display driver: replace LovyanGFX stub with hand-written ST77916 QSPI driver (ESP-IDF spi_master, quad transactions) + CH422G I2C expander for reset/backlight gating. Pixels-only in v1; CST820 touch and vendor-specific init table are follow-ups. Drops LovyanGFX from lib_deps entirely.
